       <div class="contentOcrWrapper contentOcrWrapperHover" onclick="ocr.showFullText();return false;" title="Extracted text :20 Jokes That Only intellectuals
Will Understand
1. It' s hard to explain puns to kleptomaniacs
because they always take things literally.
2. What do you get when you cross a joke with a
rhetorical question?
3. 3 logicians walk into a bar. The bartender asks
Do all of you want a drink?&quot;
The first logician says &quot;I don' t know.&quot;
The second logician says &quot;I don' t know.&quot;
The third logician says &quot;Yes!&quot;
4. Einstein, Newton and Pascal are playing hide
and go seek. It' s Einstein' s turn to count so he
covers his eyes and starts counting to ten. Pascal
runs off and hides. Newton draws a one meter by
one meter square on the ground in front of
Einstein then stands in the middle of it. Einstein
reaches ten and uncovers his eyes. He sees
Newton immediately and exclaims &quot;Newton! I
found you! You' re it!&quot;
Newton smiles and says &quot;You didn' t find me, you
found a Newton over a square meter. You found
Pascal!&quot;
5. A mathematician and an engineer agreed to
take part in an experiment. They were both placed
in a room and at the other end was a beautiful
naked woman on a bed. The experimenter said
every 30 seconds they would be allowed to travel
half the distance between themselves and the
woman. The mathematician said &quot;this is
pointless&quot; and stormed off&quot;. The engineer agreed
to go ahead with the experiment anyway. The
mathematician exclaimed on his way out &quot;don' t
you see, you' ll never actually reach her?&quot;. To
which the engineer replied, &quot;so what? Pretty soon
I' ll be close enough for all practical purposes!&quot;
6. A Roman walks into a bar and asks for a
martin's.
You mean a martini?&quot; the bartender asks.
The Roman replies, &quot;If I wanted a double, I
would have asked for it!&quot;
7. Another Roman walks into a bar, holds up
two fingers, and says, &quot;Five beers, please&quot;.
8. A Logician' s wife is having a baby. The
doctor immediately hands the newborn to the
dad.
His wife asks impatiently: &quot;So, is it a boy or a
girl&quot; 7
The logician replies: &quot;yes&quot;.
9. Sartre is sitting at a French cafe,
revising his draft of Being and Nothingness. He
says to the waitress, &quot;I' d like a cup of coffee,
please, with no cream.&quot; The waitress replies,
I' m sorry, Monsieur, but we' re out of cream.
How about with no milk?&quot;
IO. Entropy isn' t what it used to be.
11. How can you tell the difference between a
chemist and a plumber? Ask them to pronounce
unionized.
12. Why do engineers confuse Halloween and
Christmas?
Because Oct 31 = Dec 25
13. Werner Heisenberg, Kurt , and Noam
Chomsky walk into a bar. Heisenberg turns to
the other two and says, ''Clearly this is a joke,
but how can we figure out if it' s funny or not?&quot;
replies, &quot;We can' t know that because
we' re inside the joke.&quot; Chomsky says, &quot;Of course
it' s funny. You' re just telling it wrong.&quot;
14. Pavlov is sitting at a pub enjoying a pint,
the phone rings and up shouting &quot;oh
			 **** 		, I forgot to feed the dog!&quot;
15. Helium walks into a bar and orders a beer,
the bartender says, &quot;Sorry, we don' t serve noble
gases here.&quot; He doesn' t react.
16. Schrodinger: cat walks into a bar. And
doesn' t.
17. A Buddhist monk approaches a hotdog
stand and says &quot;make me one with everything&quot;.
18. A Higgs Boson walks into a church and the
priest says &quot;we don' t allow Higgs Bosons in
here&quot;. The Higgs Boson then replies &quot;but without
me, how could you have mass?&quot;
19. The programmer' s wife tells him: &quot;Run to
the store and pick up a loaf of bread. If they have
eggs, get a dozen.&quot;
The programmer comes home with 12 loaves of
bread.
20. There' s a band called . They haven' t
had any gigs yet.">

         20 Jokes That Only intellectuals

         <br/>

         <br/>

         <div class="t withAv">
          Answers:
          <br/>
          1) Kleptomaniacs steal things.
          <br/>
          2) The joke itself is a rhetorical question. A question not supposed to be answered. The only example that I can come up with "Are you stupid?" when someone stupid is showing off his stupidity
          <br/>
          3) The first logician didn't know if the other two wanted a beer. He only knew that he wanted one. If he said "No," then he didn't want one. The same goes with the second. The third one concluded that because the other two didn't say "No," then they wanted a beer, so he said yes
          <br/>
          4) A newton is a system of measurement that's equal to mass * gravity. A pascal is a newton / (1 meter squared). Newton was standing over a square 1 meter high and 1 meter width
          <br/>
          5) This is a real life equivalent of Zeno's paradox. If you want to walk to a door or something. You have to walk half the distance. Then half the remaining distance. Then half the remaining distance. And there's a mathematical proof that states you can only get to the door at infinity repetitions (half the remaining distance). The mathematician knows this and realizes this is pointless. But engineers don't really care for accuracy in their line of work. They only work toward the worst case scenarios.
          <br/>
          There's another joke that makes fun of this. A mathematician would say that pi is estimated at 3.14159... and then list as many digits as he knows. A normal person would say pi is 3.14. An engineer would say "It's around 3.14. But just in case let's call it 4."
          <br/>
          6) His fingers show the roman numeral 5
          <br/>
          7)  -- No idea (I'm not a genius. Shut up)
          <br/>
          8) Normal people will think that since the wife asked the question, she wants to know the gender of the baby. However, because she said "or." Then logicians follow a kind of a pattern. "Or" really means "If one or both of these choices are True, then the answer is true"
          <br/>
          9)  -- No idea (I'm not a genius. Shut up)
          <br/>
          <br/>
          contd
         </div>
        </div>

          <img alt="User avatar" class="av" original="http://new3.fjcdn.com/avatars/290e91_1165201.jpg" src="http://new.fjcdn.com/site/funnyjunk/images/transparent_pixel.gif"/>
          <a class="bold commentNumber" href="/Mock+iq+test/funny-pictures/5346588/15#15" id="15">
           #15
          </a>
          <a class="pink anim commentNumber" href="/Mock+iq+test/funny-pictures/5346588/14#14">

          <a class="uName" href="/user/lech" style="color:#CAE1FF;">
           lech

          <span class="date">
           (11/07/2014)
          </span>
          <span class="comExpColPanel">
           <span class="comExpCol plusButton" title="Show/Hide replies">

          <div style="clear:right">
          </div>
          <div class="t withAv">
           10) Entropy is change. I don't know how else to explain it.
           <br/>
           11) Unionized could mean two things. Union-ized. Or un-ionized. I'm not going to bore you with what they mean
           <br/>
           12) Octal is a numeric system that uses only 8 numbers. The numbers 8 and 9 don't exist in an octal system. If you want to add 7 and 1 together in octal, then the answer will be 10. It's a bit difficult to think of because we use a decimal system. If we add 7 and 1 together in decimal, the answer is 8. I'm not going to bore you with the math, but the decimal number 25 is equal to the octal number 31
           <br/>
           13)  -- No idea (I'm not a genius. Shut up)
           <br/>
           14) Pavlov did an experiment where he took a dog, and every time he rang a bell, he fed the dog. After a while, he noticed that when he rang the bell, the dog's mouth filled with saliva, even if he did not bring food to the dog. Now whenever Pavlov hears a ringing noise, he associates it with feeding his dog
           <br/>
           15) Helium is extremely stable and will never react with anything. For example Florine is extremely unstable. If left just by itself with hydrogen. It'll form hydrogen fluoride with very little energy loss
           <br/>
           16) Schrodinger's cat is a thought experiment to describe quantum mechanics. Let's say you have a cat in a box, with a vial of poison, a hammer, a geiger counter, and a radioactive isotope. Let's say that after 1 hour, the isotope has exactly 50% chance of giving off radiation, which will set off the geiger counter, which sets off the hammer, which breaks the vial, which kills the cat. After exactly 1 hour. The cat is thought to be in a superposition of both dead and alive. Only when you open the box does nature collapse the position to either dead or alive.
           <br/>
           17) A buddhist's ultimate goal is to become one with everything
           <br/>
           18) A higgs boson is an excitation of the higgs field. The higgs field is thought to give particles mass.
           <br/>
           <br/>

          <div class="t withAv">
           19) Programmers follow strict logic. She said to buy a loaf of bread, and that if they had eggs, to get a dozen. The programmer followed the sentence by saying "Alright. If they have eggs. I have to get a dozen loaves of bread. Else. I have to get one loaf of bread"
           <br/>
           <br/>
           20) This is technically not true. But only on a technicality. Let me explain it the wrong way first.
           <br/>
           In computer science, everything is stored in 1s and 0s. The maximum number of ways we can order a 1 or a 0, 10 different ways, is 2^10. This happens to be 1024 bytes. Now computer scientists use prefixes such as kilo, mega, giga, tera, and peta. 1024 bytes is 1 kilobyte (KB). 1024 kilobytes is 1 megabyte (MB). 1024 megabytes is 1 gigabyte(GB). since the band is called 1023 MB, they need 1 more megabyte to get a gig (gigabytes are informally called gigs)
           <br/>
           <br/>
           But really. 1023 MB is 1023 Megabytes which is 1023 * 1000^2 bytes. Which is 1.023 gigabytes. The correct term the post had to use is MiB. Which is kinda silly spelling, mebibyte. GiB is gibibyte. It's a very very common misconception.
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>

          <div class="t withAv">
           Take #8 for example, If you ever take a logics class
           <span class="spoiler">
            <span class="spoiler-icon">
             <!-- -->
            </span>
            <span class="spoiler-text">
             can be boring but with the right teacher it's pretty fun too.
            </span>
           </span>
           you'll that you have to define every statement as a true or false. So when she asks is the baby a boy or a girl? she's technically not asking which one is it specifically but if it is one of them. So it would return as true the baby is either a boy or a girl. What she linguistically meant to ask is "Is the baby a boy or is it a girl" that creates an option where only one of the statements can be true. Same logic for the programmer one on number 19 because eggs are there he got 12 loaves of bread what she meant to ask was get one loaf of bread and if there are eggs get 12 dozen eggs.
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>

          <div class="t withAv">
           Flamingbananas
           <br/>
           <br/>
           There are a couple of different ways of representing numbers. The one we use is called decimal. dec for short. There's a different way called octal, or oct. Now if we just look at the two words, we can see that decimal is reforming to 10 and octal to 8 (from the Latin language, of course)
           <br/>
           <br/>
           Now in the decimal system, we use 10 numbers. In the octal system, they use 8 numbers. They don't have the numbers 8 and 9. So it turns out that the decimal "25", can be converted to octal which is "31."
           <br/>
           Oct 31 is Halloween. Dec 25 is Christmas.
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
